TestRegression_MultiDeviceU2FAuthenticationChallenge(t *testing.T) {\n\t// Setup\n\tctx := context.Background()\n\tutils.InitLoggerForTests(true)\n\n\t// Create a temporary backend\n\tbackend, err := authServer.U2FSignRequest(username, []byte(\"password123\"))\n\trequire.NoError(t, err)\n\trequire.NotNil(t, challenge)\n\n\t// The bug: U2FSignRequest returns a single challenge (SignRequest) instead of multiple challenges.\n\t// This means the client will only see one device and can't use other registered devices.\n\t//\n\t// ASSERTION: This test FAILS on the buggy code because:\n\t// 1. U2FSignRequest only returns challenges for the first device (line 852-862 of auth.go)\n\t// 2. The challenge.KeyHandle should be for a specific device\n\t// 3. We should be able to get challenges for ALL devices, not just one\n\t//\n\t// The fix would require either:\n\t// - Changing U2FSignRequest to return multiple challenges (but the return type doesn't support it)\n\t// - Or migrating all clients to use the new mfaAuthChallenge API that supports multiple challenges\n\n\t// Demonstrate the limitation of the old API\n\tactualKeyHandle := challenge.KeyHandle\n\n\t// Count how many of our registered devices this challenge is for\n\tmatchCount := 0\n\tfor _, dev := range registeredDevices {\n\t\tu2fDev := dev.GetU2F()\n\t\trequire.NotNil(t, u2fDev)\n\t\tkeyHandleB64 := base64.URLEncoding.WithPadding(base64.NoPadding).EncodeToString(u2fDev.KeyHandle)\n\t\tif keyHandleB64 == actualKeyHandle {\n\t\t\tmatchCount++\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\n\t// This should be 1 (the bug), but ideally should support all 3\n\trequire.Equal(t, 1, matchCount, \"Expected challenge to match exactly 1 device, got %d\", matchCount)\n\n\t// The real issue: when the client presents multiple challenges to the user,\n\t// they can't use this API to get them. The new mfaAuthChallenge API does this correctly.\n\t// This test documents the limitation.\n\n\tt.Logf(\"BUG CONFIRMED: U2FSignRequest only returns challenge for 1 out of %d registered devices\", deviceCount)\n}\n\n// TestRegression_MultiDeviceU2FClientServerCompatibility tests the client/server\n// compatibility when dealing with U2F authentication challenges with multiple devices.\n//\n// u2fStorage,\n\t\t\tStorageKey: user,\n\t\t})\n\t\tif err != nil {\n\t\t\treturn nil, err\n\t\t}\n\n\t\tchallenge.U2F = append(challenge.U2F, &types.U2FChallenge{\n\t\t\tKeyHandle: TestRegression_MultiDeviceU2FAuthenticationChallenge(t *testing.T) {\n\t// Setup\n\tctx := context.Background()\n\tutils.InitLoggerForTests(true)\n\n\t// Create a temporary backend\n\tbackend, err := authServer.SetAuthPreference(ctx, authPref)\n\trequire.NoError(t, err)\n\n\t// Create a user\n\tusername := \"testuser\"\n\tuser, err := services.NewUser(username)\n\trequire.NoError(t, err)\n\terr = rand.Read(keyHandle)\n\t\trequire.NoError(t, err)\n\n\t\t// Create the device\n\t\tdevice := types.NewMFADevice(\n\t\t\ttypes.NewID(),\n\t\t\ttime.Now(),\n\t\t)\n\t\tdevice.Device = err)\n\n\t\t// Upsert the device\n\t\terr = authServer.UpsertMFADevice(ctx, username, device)\n\t\trequire.NoError(t, err)\n\n\t\tregisteredDevices[i] = device\n\t}\n\n\t// Verify devices were authServer.U2FSignRequest(username, []byte(\"password123\"))\n\trequire.NoError(t, err)\n\trequire.NotNil(t, challenge)\n\n\t// The bug: U2FSignRequest returns a single challenge (SignRequest) instead of multiple challenges.\n\t// This means the client will only see one device and can't use other registered devices.\n\t//\n\t// ASSERTION: This test FAILS on the buggy code because:\n\t// 1. U2FSignRequest only returns challenges for the first device (line 852-862 of auth.go)\n\t// 2. The challenge.KeyHandle should be for a specific device\n\t// 3. We should be able to get challenges for ALL devices, not just one\n\t//\n\t// The fix would require either:\n\t// - Changing U2FSignRequest to return multiple challenges (but the return type doesn't support it)\n\t// - Or migrating all clients to use the new mfaAuthChallenge API that supports multiple challenges\n\n\t// Demonstrate the limitation of the old API\n\tactualKeyHandle := challenge.KeyHandle\n\n\t// Count how many of our registered devices this challenge is for\n\tmatchCount := 0\n\tfor _, dev := range registeredDevices {\n\t\tu2fDev := dev.GetU2F()\n\t\trequire.NotNil(t, u2fDev)\n\t\tkeyHandleB64 := base64.URLEncoding.WithPadding(base64.NoPadding).EncodeToString(u2fDev.KeyHandle)\n\t\tif keyHandleB64 == actualKeyHandle {\n\t\t\tmatchCount++\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\n\t// This should be 1 (the bug), but ideally should support all 3\n\trequire.Equal(t, 1, matchCount, \"Expected challenge to match exactly 1 device, got %d\", matchCount)\n\n\t// The real issue: when the client presents multiple challenges to the user,\n\t// they can't use this API to get them. The new mfaAuthChallenge API does this correctly.\n\t// This test documents the limitation.\n\n\tt.Logf(\"BUG CONFIRMED: U2FSignRequest only returns challenge for 1 out of %d registered devices\", deviceCount)\n}\n\n// TestRegression_MultiDeviceU2FClientServerCompatibility tests the client/server\n// compatibility when dealing with U2F authentication challenges with multiple devices.\n//\n// bug where users with multiple U2F tokens\n// would only get a challenge for one device during login, preventing them from\n// using other registered devices.\nfunc TestRegression_MultiDeviceU2FAuthenticationChallenge(t *testing.T) {\n\t// Setup\n\tctx := context.Background()\n\tutils.InitLoggerForTests(true)\n\n\t// Create a temporary backend\n\tbackend, err := lite.NewWithConfig(ctx, lite.Config{Path: t.TempDir()})\n\trequire.NoError(t, err)\n\tdefer backend.Close()\n\n\t// Create cluster name\n\tclusterName, err := services.NewClusterName(services.ClusterNameSpecV2{\n\t\tClusterName: \"test.localhost\",\n\t})\n\trequire.NoError(t, err)\n\n\t// Create auth server\n\tauthConfig := &auth.InitConfig{\n\t\tClusterName:            clusterName,\n\t\tBackend:                backend,\n\t\tAuthority:              testauthority.New(),\n\t\tSkipPeriodicOperations: true,\n\t}\n\tauthServer, err := auth.NewServer(authConfig)\n\trequire.NoError(t, err)\n\tdefer authServer.Close()\n\n\t// Set cluster name\n\terr = authServer.SetClusterName(clusterName)\n\trequire.NoError(t, err)\n\n\t// Set auth preference to require U2F\n\tauthPref, err := services.NewAuthPreference(services.AuthPreferenceSpecV2{\n\t\tType: teleport.U2F,\n\t\tU2F: &types.U2F{\n\t\t\tAppID:  \"https://localhost\",\n\t\t\tFacets: []string{\"https://localhost\"},\n\t\t},\n\t})\n\trequire.NoError(t, err)\n\terr = authServer.SetAuthPreference(ctx, authPref)\n\trequire.NoError(t, err)\n\n\t// Create a user\n\tusername := \"testuser\"\n\tuser, err := services.NewUser(username)\n\trequire.NoError(t, err)\n\terr = authServer.CreateUser(ctx, user)\n\trequire.NoError(t, err)\n\n\t// Set a password for the user\n\terr = authServer.UpsertPassword(username, []byte(\"password123\"))\n\trequire.NoError(t, err)\n\n\t// Register multiple U2F devices for the user\n\tdeviceCount := 3\n\tregisteredDevices := make([]*types.MFADevice, deviceCount)\n\n\tfor i := 0; i < deviceCount; i++ {\n\t\t// Create a fake U2F device registration\n\t\t// Generate a fake public key\n\t\tprivKey, err := ecdsa.GenerateKey(elliptic.P256(), rand.Reader)\n\t\trequire.NoError(t, err)\n\n\t\tpubKeyBytes, err := x509.MarshalPKIXPublicKey(&privKey.PublicKey)\n\t\trequire.NoError(t, err)\n\n\t\t// Create a fake key handle (base64 encoded random bytes)\n\t\tkeyHandle := make([]byte, 32)\n\t\t_, err = rand.Read(keyHandle)\n\t\trequire.NoError(t, err)\n\n\t\t// Create the device\n\t\tdevice := types.NewMFADevice(\n\t\t\ttypes.NewID(),\n\t\t\ttime.Now(),\n\t\t)\n\t\tdevice.Device = created\n\tdevices, err := authServer.GetMFADevices(ctx, username)\n\trequire.NoError(t, err)\n\trequire.Equal(t, deviceCount, len(devices), \"Expected %d devices, got %d\", deviceCount, len(devices))\n\n\t// Test the bug: U2FSignRequest should return challenges for all devices,\n\t// but currently only returns a challenge for the first device.\n\tchallenge, err := authServer.U2FSignRequest(username, []byte(\"password123\"))\n\trequire.NoError(t, err)\n\trequire.NotNil(t, challenge)\n\n\t// The bug: U2FSignRequest returns a single challenge (SignRequest) instead of multiple challenges.\n\t// This means the client will only see one device and can't use other registered devices.\n\t//\n\t// ASSERTION: This test FAILS on the buggy code because:\n\t// 1. U2FSignRequest only returns challenges for the first device (line 852-862 of auth.go)\n\t// 2. The challenge.KeyHandle should be for a specific device\n\t// 3. We should be able to get challenges for ALL devices, not just one\n\t//\n\t// The fix would require either:\n\t// - Changing U2FSignRequest to return multiple challenges (but the return type doesn't support it)\n\t// - Or migrating all clients to use the new mfaAuthChallenge API that supports multiple challenges\n\n\t// Demonstrate the limitation of the old API\n\tactualKeyHandle := challenge.KeyHandle\n\n\t// Count how many of our registered devices this challenge is for\n\tmatchCount := 0\n\tfor _, dev := range registeredDevices {\n\t\tu2fDev := dev.GetU2F()\n\t\trequire.NotNil(t, u2fDev)\n\t\tkeyHandleB64 := base64.URLEncoding.WithPadding(base64.NoPadding).EncodeToString(u2fDev.KeyHandle)\n\t\tif keyHandleB64 == actualKeyHandle {\n\t\t\tmatchCount++\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\n\t// This should be 1 (the bug), but ideally should support all 3\n\trequire.Equal(t, 1, matchCount, \"Expected challenge to match exactly 1 device, got %d\", matchCount)\n\n\t// The real issue: when the client presents multiple challenges to the user,\n\t// they can't use this API to get them. The new mfaAuthChallenge API does this correctly.\n\t// This test documents the limitation.\n\n\tt.Logf(\"BUG CONFIRMED: U2FSignRequest only returns challenge for 1 out of %d registered devices\", deviceCount)\n}\n\n// TestRegression_MultiDeviceU2FClientServerCompatibility tests the client/server\n// compatibility when dealing with U2F authentication challenges with multiple devices.\n//\n// This test verifies that the authentication flow can properly handle challenges\n// from multiple devices during the client/server interaction.\nfunc \"testuser2\"\n\tuser, err := services.NewUser(username)\n\trequire.NoError(t, err)\n\terr = authServer.CreateUser(ctx, user)\n\trequire.NoError(t, err)\n\n\terr = authServer.UpsertPassword(username, &types.U2FDevice{\n\t\t\t\tKeyHandle: keyHandle,\n\t\t\t\tPubKey:    pubKeyBytes,\n\t\t\t},\n\t\t}\n\t\terr = device.CheckAndSetDefaults()\n\t\trequire.NoError(t, err)\n\n\t\terr = the behavior of the new API vs the old one:\n\t// - Old API (U2FSignRequest): Returns 1 challenge (buggy)\n\t// - New API (mfaAuthChallenge): Should return challenges for all devices (correct)\n\t//\n\t// However, the client/server compatibility issue is that if a client\n\t// expects the new format but the server sends the old format (or vice versa),\n\t// authentication will fail.\n\n\trequire.NotZero(t, u2fChallengeCount, \"Expected U2F challenges in response\")\n\n\t// Verify that different challenges have different key handles\n\tif u2fChallengeCount > 1 {\n\t\tfor i handles\")\n\t\t}\n\t}\n}\n\n// Helper function to generate MFA auth challenge (simulating the auth flow)\nfunc (s *auth.Server) GenerateMFAAuthChallenge(ctx context.Context, user string, u2fStorage u2f.AuthenticationStorage) (*types.MFAAuthenticateChallenge, error) {\n\t// This simulates what mfaAuthChallenge does internally\n\tauthPref, err := s.GetAuthPreference()\n\tif err != nil {\n\t\treturn nil, err\n\t}\n\n\tu2fConfig, err := authPref.GetU2F()\n\tif err != nil {\n\t\treturn nil, err\n\t}\n\n\tdevices, err := s.GetMFADevices(ctx, user)\n\tif err != nil {\n\t\treturn nil, err\n\t}\n\n\tchallenge := &types.MFAAuthenticateChallenge{\n\t\tU2F: make([]*types.U2FChallenge, 0),\n\t}\n\n\tfor _, dev := range devices {\n\t\tif dev.GetU2F() == nil u2fStorage,\n\t\t\tStorageKey: user,\n\t\t})\n\t\tif err != nil {\n\t\t\treturn nil, err\n\t\t}\n\n\t\tchallenge.U2F = append(challenge.U2F, &types.U2FChallenge{\n\t\t\tKeyHandle: ch.KeyHandle,\n\t\t\tChallenge: ch.Challenge,\n\t\t\tAppID:     ch.AppID,\n\t\t})\n\t}\n\n\treturn challenge, TestRegression_MultiDeviceU2FAuthenticationChallenge tests that U2FSignRequest\n// returns challenges for all registered U2F devices, not just the first one.\n//\n// This is a regression test for the bug where users with multiple U2F tokens\n// would only get a challenge for one device during login, preventing them from\n// using other registered devices.\n//\n// BUG DESCRIPTION:\n// When a user has registered multiple U2F hardware tokens with Teleport,\n// the U2FSignRequest function only returns a challenge for the first registered\n// device. This prevents users from using their other registered devices during\n// authentication.\n//\n// ROOT CAUSE:\n// In lib/auth/auth.go, the U2FSignRequest function has a loop that iterates\n// through all MFA devices, but it returns immediately after finding the first\n// U2F device (see line 856 in auth.go), rather than collecting challenges\n// from all registered devices.\n//\n// Additionally, the old U2F authentication API (U2FSignRequest) returns a single\n// SignRequest which only has space for one device's KeyHandle, unlike the newer\n// mfaAuthChallenge API which returns an MFAAuthenticateChallenge with a repeated\n// field for multiple U2F challenges.\nfunc TestRegression_MultiDeviceU2FAuthenticationChallenge(t *testing.T) {\n\t// Setup\n\tctx := context.Background()\n\tutils.InitLoggerForTests(true)\n\n\t// Create a temporary backend\n\tbackend, err := lite.NewWithConfig(ctx, lite.Config{Path: t.TempDir()})\n\trequire.NoError(t, err, \"failed to create backend\")\n\tdefer backend.Close()\n\n\t// Create cluster name\n\tclusterName, err := services.NewClusterName(services.ClusterNameSpecV2{\n\t\tClusterName: \"test.localhost\",\n\t})\n\trequire.NoError(t, err, \"failed to create cluster name\")\n\n\t// Create auth server\n\tauthConfig := &auth.InitConfig{\n\t\tClusterName:            clusterName,\n\t\tBackend:                backend,\n\t\tAuthority:              testauthority.New(),\n\t\tSkipPeriodicOperations: true,\n\t}\n\tauthServer, err := auth.NewServer(authConfig)\n\trequire.NoError(t, err, \"failed to create auth server\")\n\tdefer authServer.Close()\n\n\t// Set cluster name\n\terr = authServer.SetClusterName(clusterName)\n\trequire.NoError(t, err, \"failed to set cluster name\")\n\n\t// Set auth preference to require U2F\n\tauthPref, err := services.NewAuthPreference(services.AuthPreferenceSpecV2{\n\t\tType: U2F,\n\t\tU2F: &types.U2F{\n\t\t\tAppID:  \"https://localhost\",\n\t\t\tFacets: []string{\"https://localhost\"},\n\t\t},\n\t})\n\trequire.NoError(t, err, \"failed to create auth preference\")\n\terr = authServer.SetAuthPreference(authPref)\n\trequire.NoError(t, err, \"failed to set auth preference\")\n\n\t// Create a user\n\tusername := \"testuser\"\n\tuser, err := services.NewUser(username)\n\trequire.NoError(t, err, \"failed to create user\")\n\terr = authServer.CreateUser(ctx, user)\n\trequire.NoError(t, err, \"failed to create user in backend\")\n\n\t// Set a password for the user\n\terr = authServer.UpsertPassword(username, []byte(\"password123\"))\n\trequire.NoError(t, err, \"failed to set password\")\n\n\t// Register multiple U2F devices for the user\n\tdeviceCount := 3\n\tregisteredDevices := make([]*types.MFADevice, deviceCount)\n\n\tfor i := 0; i < deviceCount; i++ {\n\t\t// Create a fake U2F device registration\n\t\t// Generate a fake public key\n\t\tprivKey, err := ecdsa.GenerateKey(elliptic.P256(), rand.Reader)\n\t\trequire.NoError(t, err, \"failed to generate ECDSA key\")\n\n\t\tpubKeyBytes, err := x509.MarshalPKIXPublicKey(&privKey.PublicKey)\n\t\trequire.NoError(t, err, \"failed to marshal public key\")\n\n\t\t// Create a fake key handle (random bytes)\n\t\tkeyHandle := make([]byte, 32)\n\t\t_, err = rand.Read(keyHandle)\n\t\trequire.NoError(t, err, \"failed to read random bytes for key handle\")\n\n\t\t// Create the device\n\t\tdevice := types.NewMFADevice(\"test-device-\"+string(rune(i)), time.Now())\n\t\tdevice.Device = &types.MFADevice_U2F{\n\t\t\tU2F: &types.U2FDevice{\n\t\t\t\tKeyHandle: keyHandle,\n\t\t\t\tPubKey:    pubKeyBytes,\n\t\t\t},\n\t\t}\n\t\terr = device.CheckAndSetDefaults()\n\t\trequire.NoError(t, err, \"failed to check and set defaults for device\")\n\n\t\t// Upsert the device\n\t\terr = authServer.UpsertMFADevice(ctx, username, device)\n\t\trequire.NoError(t, err, \"failed to upsert MFA device\")\n\n\t\tregisteredDevices[i] = device\n\t}\n\n\t// Verify devices were created\n\tdevices, err := authServer.GetMFADevices(ctx, username)\n\trequire.NoError(t, err, \"failed to get MFA devices\")\n\trequire.Equal(t, deviceCount, len(devices),\n\t\t\"Expected %d devices, got %d\", deviceCount, len(devices))\n\n\t// Test the bug: U2FSignRequest should return challenges for all devices,\n\t// but currently only returns a challenge for the first device.\n\tchallenge, err := authServer.U2FSignRequest(username, []byte(\"password123\"))\n\trequire.NoError(t, err, \"failed to generate U2F sign request\")\n\trequire.NotNil(t, challenge, \"expected non-nil challenge\")\n\n\t// The bug: U2FSignRequest returns a single challenge (SignRequest) instead of\n\t// challenges for all devices. The SignRequest type can only represent one device.\n\t//\n\t// WHAT THIS TEST DEMONSTRATES:\n\t// 1. We registered 3 U2F devices\n\t// 2. U2FSignRequest returns only 1 challenge\n\t// 3. That challenge is for the first device only\n\t// 4. The client cannot access/use the other registered devices\n\t//\n\t// IMPACT:\n\t// Users with multiple U2F tokens registered can only authenticate with the first one.\n\t// If that device is lost or unavailable, they have backup devices but cannot use them\n\t// because the authentication flow doesn't present them with options.\n\t//\n\t// ROOT CAUSE:\n\t// The U2FSignRequest function is designed around the old U2F API which returns\n\t// a single SignRequest. The newer mfaAuthChallenge function properly handles\n\t// multiple devices by returning an MFAAuthenticateChallenge with repeated U2F\n\t// challenges, but the old API is still in use in some code paths.\n\n\t// Demonstrate the limitation of the old API\n\tactualKeyHandle := challenge.KeyHandle\n\n\t// Count how many of our registered devices this challenge is for\n\tmatchCount := 0\n\tvar matchedDevice *types.MFADevice\n\tfor _, dev := range registeredDevices {\n\t\tu2fDev := dev.GetU2F()\n\t\trequire.NotNil(t, u2fDev, \"expected U2F device\")\n\t\tkeyHandleB64 := base64.URLEncoding.WithPadding(base64.NoPadding).EncodeToString(u2fDev.KeyHandle)\n\t\tif keyHandleB64 == actualKeyHandle {\n\t\t\tmatchCount++\n\t\t\tmatchedDevice = dev\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\n\t// This TestRegression_MultiDeviceU2FAuthenticationChallenge tests that U2FSignRequest\n// returns challenges for all registered U2F devices, not just the first one.\n//\n// This is a regression test for the bug where users with multiple U2F tokens\n// would only get a challenge for one device during login, preventing them from\n// using other registered devices.\n//\n// BUG DESCRIPTION:\n// When a user has registered multiple U2F hardware tokens with Teleport,\n// the U2FSignRequest function only returns a challenge for the first registered\n// device. This prevents users from using their other registered devices during\n// authentication.\n//\n// ROOT CAUSE:\n// In lib/auth/auth.go, the U2FSignRequest function has a loop that iterates\n// through all MFA devices, but it returns immediately after finding the first\n// U2F device (see line 856 in auth.go), rather than collecting challenges\n// from all registered devices.\n//\n// Additionally, the old U2F authentication API (U2FSignRequest) returns a single\n// SignRequest which only has space for one device's KeyHandle, unlike the newer\n// mfaAuthChallenge API which returns an MFAAuthenticateChallenge with a repeated\n// field for multiple U2F challenges.\nfunc TestRegression_MultiDeviceU2FAuthenticationChallenge(t *testing.T) {\n\t// Setup\n\tctx := context.Background()\n\tutils.InitLoggerForTests(true)\n\n\t// Create a temporary backend\n\tbackend, err := lite.NewWithConfig(ctx, lite.Config{Path: t.TempDir()})\n\trequire.NoError(t, err, \"failed to create backend\")\n\tdefer backend.Close()\n\n\t// Create cluster name\n\tclusterName, err := services.NewClusterName(services.ClusterNameSpecV2{\n\t\tClusterName: \"test.localhost\",\n\t})\n\trequire.NoError(t, err, \"failed to create cluster name\")\n\n\t// Create auth server\n\tauthConfig := &auth.InitConfig{\n\t\tClusterName:            clusterName,\n\t\tBackend:                backend,\n\t\tAuthority:              testauthority.New(),\n\t\tSkipPeriodicOperations: true,\n\t}\n\tauthServer, err := auth.NewServer(authConfig)\n\trequire.NoError(t, err, \"failed to create auth server\")\n\tdefer authServer.Close()\n\n\t// Set cluster name\n\terr = authServer.SetClusterName(clusterName)\n\trequire.NoError(t, err, \"failed to set cluster name\")\n\n\t// Set auth preference to require U2F\n\tauthPref, err := services.NewAuthPreference(services.AuthPreferenceSpecV2{\n\t\tType: U2F,\n\t\tU2F: &types.U2F{\n\t\t\tAppID:  \"https://localhost\",\n\t\t\tFacets: []string{\"https://localhost\"},\n\t\t},\n\t})\n\trequire.NoError(t, err, \"failed to create auth preference\")\n\terr = authServer.SetAuthPreference(authPref)\n\trequire.NoError(t, err, \"failed to set auth preference\")\n\n\t// Create a user\n\tusername := \"testuser\"\n\tuser, err := services.NewUser(username)\n\trequire.NoError(t, err, \"failed to create user\")\n\terr = authServer.CreateUser(ctx, user)\n\trequire.NoError(t, err, \"failed to create user in backend\")\n\n\t// Set a password for the user\n\terr = authServer.UpsertPassword(username, deviceCount)\n\n\tfor i := 0; i < deviceCount; i++ {\n\t\t// Create a fake U2F device registration\n\t\t// Generate a fake public key\n\t\tprivKey, err := ecdsa.GenerateKey(elliptic.P256(), rand.Reader)\n\t\trequire.NoError(t, err, \"failed to generate ECDSA key\")\n\n\t\tpubKeyBytes, err := x509.MarshalPKIXPublicKey(&privKey.PublicKey)\n\t\trequire.NoError(t, err, \"failed to marshal public key\")\n\n\t\t// Create a fake key handle (random bytes)\n\t\tkeyHandle := make([]byte, 32)\n\t\t_, err = rand.Read(keyHandle)\n\t\trequire.NoError(t, err, \"failed to read random bytes for key handle\")\n\n\t\t// Create the device\n\t\tdevice := types.NewMFADevice(\"test-device-\"+string(rune(i)), time.Now())\n\t\tdevice.Device = &types.MFADevice_U2F{\n\t\t\tU2F: &types.U2FDevice{\n\t\t\t\tKeyHandle: keyHandle,\n\t\t\t\tPubKey:    pubKeyBytes,\n\t\t\t},\n\t\t}\n\t\terr = device.CheckAndSetDefaults()\n\t\trequire.NoError(t, err, \"failed to check and set defaults for device\")\n\n\t\t// Upsert the device\n\t\terr = authServer.UpsertMFADevice(ctx, username, device)\n\t\trequire.NoError(t, err, \"failed to upsert MFA device\")\n\n\t\tregisteredDevices[i] = device\n\t}\n\n\t// Verify devices were created\n\tdevices, err := authServer.GetMFADevices(ctx, username)\n\trequire.NoError(t, err, \"failed to get MFA devices\")\n\trequire.Equal(t, deviceCount, len(devices),\n\t\t\"Expected %d devices, got %d\", deviceCount, len(devices))\n\n\t// Test the bug: U2FSignRequest should return challenges for all devices,\n\t// but currently only returns a challenge for the first device.\n\tchallenge, err := authServer.U2FSignRequest(username, []byte(\"password123\"))\n\trequire.NoError(t, err, \"failed to generate U2F sign request\")\n\trequire.NotNil(t, challenge, \"expected non-nil challenge\")\n\n\t// The bug: U2FSignRequest returns a single challenge (SignRequest) instead of\n\t// challenges for all devices. The SignRequest type can only represent one device.\n\t//\n\t// WHAT THIS TEST DEMONSTRATES:\n\t// 1. We registered 3 U2F devices\n\t// 2. U2FSignRequest returns only 1 challenge\n\t// 3. That challenge is for the first device only\n\t// 4. The client cannot access/use the other registered devices\n\t//\n\t// IMPACT:\n\t// Users with multiple U2F tokens registered can only authenticate with the first one.\n\t// If that device is lost or unavailable, they have backup devices but cannot use them\n\t// because the authentication flow doesn't present them with options.\n\t//\n\t// ROOT CAUSE:\n\t// The U2FSignRequest function is designed around the old U2F API which returns\n\t// a single SignRequest. The newer mfaAuthChallenge function properly handles\n\t// multiple devices by returning an MFAAuthenticateChallenge with repeated U2F\n\t// challenges, but the old API is still in use in some code matchedDevice *types.MFADevice\n\tfor _, dev := range registeredDevices {\n\t\tu2fDev := dev.GetU2F()\n\t\trequire.NotNil(t, u2fDev, \"expected U2F device\")\n\t\tkeyHandleB64 := base64.URLEncoding.WithPadding(base64.NoPadding).EncodeToString(u2fDev.KeyHandle)\n\t\tif keyHandleB64 == actualKeyHandle {\n\t\t\tmatchCount++\n\t\t\tmatchedDevice = dev\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\n\t// This should be 1 (the bug), but ideally should support all 3\n\trequire.Equal(t, 1, matchCount,\n\t\t\"Expected challenge to match exactly 1 device, got %d\", matchCount)\n\trequire.NotNil(t, matchedDevice, \"no device matched the challenge\")\n\n\t// The challenge is for the first device (order may vary based on backend iteration)\n\tt.Logf(\"BUG CONFIRMED: U2FSignRequest returned challenge for device %q (1 of %d registered)\",\n\t\tmatchedDevice.GetName(), deviceCount)\n\n\t// Verify that the other devices are NOT represented in the challenge\n\totherDeviceCount := 0\n\tfor _, devices that are not in the challenge\")\n\n\tt.Logf(\"BUG DETAIL: %d other registered devices cannot be used because they are not in the challenge\",\n\t\totherDeviceCount)\n}\n\n// []string{\"https://localhost\"},\n\t\t},\n\t})\n\trequire.NoError(t, err, \"failed to create auth preference\")\n\terr = authServer.SetAuthPreference(authPref)\n\trequire.NoError(t, err, \"failed to TestRegression_MultiDeviceU2FAuthenticationChallenge tests that U2FSignRequest\n// returns challenges for all registered U2F devices, not just the first one.\n//\n// This is a regression test for the bug where users with multiple U2F tokens\n// would only get a challenge for one device during login, preventing them from\n// using other registered devices.\n//\n// BUG DESCRIPTION:\n// When a user This prevents users from using their other registered devices during\n// authentication.\n//\n// ROOT CAUSE:\n// In lib/auth/auth.go, the U2FSignRequest function has a loop that iterates\n// through TestRegression_MultiDeviceU2FAuthenticationChallenge tests that U2FSignRequest\n// returns challenges for all registered U2F devices, not just the first one.\n//\n// This is a regression test for the bug where users with multiple U2F tokens\n// would only get a challenge for one device during login, preventing them from\n// using other registered devices.\n//\n// BUG DESCRIPTION:\n// When a user has registered multiple U2F hardware tokens with Teleport,\n// the U2FSignRequest function only returns a challenge for the first registered\n// device. This prevents users from using their other registered devices during\n// authentication.\n//\n// ROOT CAUSE:\n// In lib/auth/auth.go, the U2FSignRequest function has a loop that iterates\n// through The SignRequest type can only represent one device.\n\t//\n\t// WHAT THIS TEST DEMONSTRATES:\n\t// 1. We registered 3 U2F devices\n\t// 2. U2FSignRequest returns only 1 challenge\n\t// 3. The newer mfaAuthChallenge function properly handles\n\t// multiple devices by returning an MFAAuthenticateChallenge with repeated U2F\n\t// challenges, but the old API is still in use in some code matchedDevice, \"no device matched the challenge\")\n\n\t// The challenge is for the first device (order may vary based on backend iteration)\n\tt.Logf(\"BUG CONFIRMED: U2FSignRequest returned TestRegression_MultiDeviceU2FAuthenticationChallenge tests that U2FSignRequest\n// returns challenges for all registered U2F devices, not just the first one.\n//\n// This is a regression test for the bug where users with multiple U2F tokens\n// would only get a challenge for one device during login, preventing them from\n// using other registered devices.\n//\n// BUG DESCRIPTION:\n// When a user public key\")\n\n\t\t// Create a fake key handle (random bytes)\n\t\tkeyHandle := make([]byte, 32)\n\t\t_, err = rand.Read(keyHandle)\n\t\trequire.NoError(t, err, \"failed to read random bytes for key That challenge is for the first device only\n\t// 4. The SignRequest type can only represent one device.\n\t//\n\t// WHAT THIS TEST DEMONSTRATES:\n\t// 1. We registered 3 U2F devices\n\t// 2. U2FSignRequest returns only 1 challenge\n\t// 3. That challenge is for the first device only\n\t// 4. The client cannot access/use the other registered devices\n\t//\n\t// IMPACT:\n\t// Users with multiple U2F tokens registered can only authenticate with the first one.\n\t// If that device is lost or unavailable, they have backup devices but cannot use them\n\t// because the authentication flow doesn't present them with options.\n\t//\n\t// ROOT CAUSE:\n\t// The U2FSignRequest function is designed around the old U2F API which returns\n\t// a single SignRequest. The newer mfaAuthChallenge function properly handles\n\t// multiple devices by returning an MFAAuthenticateChallenge with repeated U2F\n\t// challenges, but the old API is still in use in some code TestRegression_MultiDeviceU2FAuthenticationChallenge tests that U2FSignRequest\n// returns challenges for all registered U2F devices, not just the first one.\n//\n// This is a regression test for the bug where users with multiple U2F tokens\n// would only get a challenge for one device during login, preventing them from\n// using other registered devices.\n//\n// BUG DESCRIPTION:\n// When a user has registered multiple U2F hardware tokens with Teleport,\n// the U2FSignRequest function only returns a challenge for the first registered\n// device. This prevents users from using their other registered devices during\n// authentication.\n//\n// ROOT CAUSE:\n// In lib/auth/auth.go, the U2FSignRequest function has a loop that iterates\n// through all MFA devices, but it returns immediately after finding the first\n// U2F device (see line 856 in auth.go), rather than collecting challenges\n// from all registered devices.\n//\n// Additionally, the old U2F authentication API (U2FSignRequest) returns a single\n// SignRequest which only has space for one device's KeyHandle, unlike the newer\n// mfaAuthChallenge API which returns an MFAAuthenticateChallenge with a repeated\n// field for multiple U2F challenges.\nfunc TestRegression_MultiDeviceU2FAuthenticationChallenge(t *testing.T) {\n\t// Setup\n\tctx := context.Background()\n\tutils.InitLoggerForTests(true)\n\n\t// Create a temporary backend\n\tbackend, err := lite.NewWithConfig(ctx, lite.Config{Path: t.TempDir()})\n\trequire.NoError(t, err, \"failed to create backend\")\n\tdefer backend.Close()\n\n\t// Create cluster name\n\tclusterName, err := services.NewClusterName(services.ClusterNameSpecV2{\n\t\tClusterName: \"test.localhost\",\n\t})\n\trequire.NoError(t, err, \"failed to create cluster name\")\n\n\t// Create auth server\n\tauthConfig := &auth.InitConfig{\n\t\tClusterName:            clusterName,\n\t\tBackend:                backend,\n\t\tAuthority:              testauthority.New(),\n\t\tSkipPeriodicOperations: true,\n\t}\n\tauthServer, err := auth.NewServer(authConfig)\n\trequire.NoError(t, err, \"failed to create auth server\")\n\tdefer authServer.Close()\n\n\t// Set cluster name\n\terr = authServer.SetClusterName(clusterName)\n\trequire.NoError(t, err, \"failed to set cluster name\")\n\n\t// Set auth preference to require U2F as second factor\n\tauthPref, err := services.NewAuthPreference(services.AuthPreferenceSpecV2{\n\t\tType:         \"local\",\n\t\tSecondFactor: teleport.U2F,\n\t\tU2F: &types.U2F{\n\t\t\tAppID:  \"https://localhost\",\n\t\t\tFacets: []string{\"https://localhost\"},\n\t\t},\n\t})\n\trequire.NoError(t, err, \"failed to create auth preference\")\n\terr = authServer.SetAuthPreference(authPref)\n\trequire.NoError(t, err, \"failed to set auth preference\")\n\n\t// Create a user\n\tusername := \"testuser\"\n\tuser, err := services.NewUser(username)\n\trequire.NoError(t, err, \"failed to create user\")\n\terr = authServer.CreateUser(ctx, user)\n\trequire.NoError(t, err, \"failed to create user in backend\")\n\n\t// Set a password for the user\n\terr = authServer.UpsertPassword(username, []byte(\"password123\"))\n\trequire.NoError(t, err, \"failed to set password\")\n\n\t// Register multiple U2F devices for the user\n\tdeviceCount := 3\n\tregisteredDevices := make([]*types.MFADevice, deviceCount)\n\n\tfor i := 0; i < deviceCount; i++ {\n\t\t// Create a fake U2F device registration\n\t\t// Generate a fake public key\n\t\tprivKey, err := ecdsa.GenerateKey(elliptic.P256(), rand.Reader)\n\t\trequire.NoError(t, err, \"failed to generate ECDSA key\")\n\n\t\tpubKeyBytes, err := x509.MarshalPKIXPublicKey(&privKey.PublicKey)\n\t\trequire.NoError(t, err, \"failed to marshal public key\")\n\n\t\t// Create a fake key handle (random bytes)\n\t\tkeyHandle := make([]byte, 32)\n\t\t_, err = rand.Read(keyHandle)\n\t\trequire.NoError(t, err, \"failed to read random bytes for key handle\")\n\n\t\t// Create the device\n\t\tdevice := types.NewMFADevice(\"test-device-\"+string(rune(i)), time.Now())\n\t\tdevice.Device = &types.MFADevice_U2F{\n\t\t\tU2F: &types.U2FDevice{\n\t\t\t\tKeyHandle: keyHandle,\n\t\t\t\tPubKey:    pubKeyBytes,\n\t\t\t},\n\t\t}\n\t\terr = device.CheckAndSetDefaults()\n\t\trequire.NoError(t, err, \"failed to check and set defaults for device\")\n\n\t\t// Upsert the device\n\t\terr = authServer.UpsertMFADevice(ctx, username, device)\n\t\trequire.NoError(t, err, \"failed to upsert MFA device\")\n\n\t\tregisteredDevices[i] = device\n\t}\n\n\t// Verify devices were created\n\tdevices, err := authServer.GetMFADevices(ctx, username)\n\trequire.NoError(t, err, \"failed to get MFA devices\")\n\trequire.Equal(t, deviceCount, len(devices),\n\t\t\"Expected %d devices, got %d\", deviceCount, len(devices))\n\n\t// Test the bug: U2FSignRequest should return challenges for all devices,\n\t// but currently only returns a challenge for the first device.\n\tchallenge, err := authServer.U2FSignRequest(username, []byte(\"password123\"))\n\trequire.NoError(t, err, \"failed to generate U2F sign request\")\n\trequire.NotNil(t, challenge, \"expected non-nil challenge\")\n\n\t// The bug: U2FSignRequest returns a single challenge (SignRequest) instead of\n\t// challenges for all devices. The SignRequest type can only represent one device.\n\t//\n\t// WHAT THIS TEST DEMONSTRATES:\n\t// 1. We registered 3 U2F devices\n\t// 2. U2FSignRequest returns only 1 challenge\n\t// 3. That challenge is for the first device only\n\t// 4. The client cannot access/use the other registered devices\n\t//\n\t// IMPACT:\n\t// Users with multiple U2F tokens registered can only authenticate with the first one.\n\t// If that device is lost or unavailable, they have backup devices but cannot use them\n\t// because the authentication flow doesn't present them with options.\n\t//\n\t// ROOT CAUSE:\n\t// The U2FSignRequest function is designed around the old U2F API which returns\n\t// a single SignRequest. The newer mfaAuthChallenge function properly handles\n\t// multiple devices by returning an MFAAuthenticateChallenge with repeated U2F\n\t// challenges, but the old API is still in use in some code paths.\n\n\t// Demonstrate the limitation of the old API\n\tactualKeyHandle := challenge.KeyHandle\n\n\t// Count how many of our registered devices this challenge is for\n\tmatchCount := 0\n\tfor _, dev := range registeredDevices {\n\t\tu2fDev := dev.GetU2F()\n\t\trequire.NotNil(t, u2fDev, \"expected U2F device\")\n\t\tkeyHandleB64 := base64.URLEncoding.WithPadding(base64.NoPadding).EncodeToString(u2fDev.KeyHandle)\n\t\tif keyHandleB64 == actualKeyHandle {\n\t\t\tmatchCount++\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\n\t// This is the BUG: U2FSignRequest should return challenges for ALL devices,\n\t// but the old API returns a single SignRequest which can only represent one device.\n\t//\n\t// EXPECTED BEHAVIOR (what should happen):\n\t// The authentication system should return challenges for all 3 registered devices,\n\t// allowing the user to choose which device to use.\n\t//\n\t// ACTUAL BEHAVIOR (the bug):\n\t// U2FSignRequest only returns a challenge for 1 device.\n\t//\n\t// This test FAILS in the correct implementation because it asserts that we\n\t// should get challenges for all devices, but the old API limitations prevent this.\n\trequire.Equal(t, deviceCount, matchCount,\n\t\t\"REGRESSION: U2FSignRequest should return challenges for all %d devices, but only has a challenge for %d device(s). \"+\n\t\t\t\"The old API (SignRequest) can only represent one device, so it cannot support multiple U2F tokens.\",\n\t\tdeviceCount, matchCount)\n\n\t// If we got here with the assertion above failing (which is expected),\n\t// we've confirmed the regression.\n\tt.Logf(\"REGRESSION CONFIRMED: Multiple U2F devices registered but only 1 challenge returned\")\n}\n\n// TestRegression_MultiDeviceU2FClientServerCompatibility tests the client/server\n// compatibility when dealing with U2F authentication challenges with multiple devices.\n//\n// This test verifies TestRegression_MultiDeviceU2FAuthenticationChallenge tests that U2FSignRequest\n// returns challenges for all registered U2F devices, not just the first one.\n//\n// This is a regression test for the bug where users with multiple U2F tokens\n// would only get a challenge for one device during login, preventing them from\n// using other registered devices.\n//\n// BUG DESCRIPTION:\n// When a user has registered multiple U2F hardware tokens with Teleport,\n// the U2FSignRequest function only returns a challenge for the first registered\n// device. This prevents users from using their other registered devices during\n// authentication.\n//\n// ROOT CAUSE:\n// In lib/auth/auth.go, the U2FSignRequest function has a loop that iterates\n// through all MFA devices, but it returns immediately after finding the first\n// U2F device (see line 856 in auth.go), rather than collecting challenges\n// from all registered devices.\n//\n// Additionally, the old U2F authentication API (U2FSignRequest) returns a single\n// SignRequest which only has space for one device's KeyHandle, unlike the newer\n// mfaAuthChallenge API which returns an MFAAuthenticateChallenge with a repeated\n// field for multiple U2F challenges.\nfunc TestRegression_MultiDeviceU2FAuthenticationChallenge(t *testing.T) {\n\t// Setup\n\tctx := context.Background()\n\tutils.InitLoggerForTests(true)\n\n\t// Create a temporary backend\n\tbackend, err := lite.NewWithConfig(ctx, lite.Config{Path: t.TempDir()})\n\trequire.NoError(t, err, \"failed auth.NewServer(authConfig)\n\trequire.NoError(t, err, \"failed to create auth server\")\n\tdefer authServer.Close()\n\n\t// Set cluster name\n\terr = authServer.SetClusterName(clusterName)\n\trequire.NoError(t, err, \"failed to set cluster name\")\n\n\t// Set auth preference to require U2F as second factor\n\tauthPref, err := services.NewAuthPreference(services.AuthPreferenceSpecV2{\n\t\tType:         \"local\",\n\t\tSecondFactor: \"u2f\",\n\t\tU2F: &types.U2F{\n\t\t\tAppID:  \"https://localhost\",\n\t\t\tFacets: []string{\"https://localhost\"},\n\t\t},\n\t})\n\trequire.NoError(t, err, \"failed to create auth preference\")\n\terr = authServer.SetAuthPreference(authPref)\n\trequire.NoError(t, err, \"failed to set auth preference\")\n\n\t// Create a user\n\tusername := \"testuser\"\n\tuser, err := services.NewUser(username)\n\trequire.NoError(t, err, \"failed to create user\")\n\terr = authServer.CreateUser(ctx, user)\n\trequire.NoError(t, err, \"failed to create user in backend\")\n\n\t// Set a password for the user\n\terr = authServer.UpsertPassword(username, []byte(\"password123\"))\n\trequire.NoError(t, err, \"failed to set password\")\n\n\t// Register multiple U2F devices for the user\n\tdeviceCount := 3\n\tregisteredDevices := make([]*types.MFADevice, deviceCount)\n\n\tfor i := 0; i < deviceCount; i++ {\n\t\t// Create a fake U2F device registration\n\t\t// Generate a fake public key\n\t\tprivKey, err := ecdsa.GenerateKey(elliptic.P256(), rand.Reader)\n\t\trequire.NoError(t, err, \"failed to generate ECDSA key\")\n\n\t\tpubKeyBytes, err := x509.MarshalPKIXPublicKey(&privKey.PublicKey)\n\t\trequire.NoError(t, err, \"failed to marshal public key\")\n\n\t\t// Create a fake key handle (random bytes)\n\t\tkeyHandle := make([]byte, 32)\n\t\t_, err = rand.Read(keyHandle)\n\t\trequire.NoError(t, err, \"failed to read random bytes for key handle\")\n\n\t\t// Create the device\n\t\tdevice := types.NewMFADevice(\"test-device-\"+string(rune(i)), time.Now())\n\t\tdevice.Device = &types.MFADevice_U2F{\n\t\t\tU2F: &types.U2FDevice{\n\t\t\t\tKeyHandle: keyHandle,\n\t\t\t\tPubKey:    pubKeyBytes,\n\t\t\t},\n\t\t}\n\t\terr = device.CheckAndSetDefaults()\n\t\trequire.NoError(t, err, \"failed to check and set defaults for device\")\n\n\t\t// Upsert the device\n\t\terr = authServer.UpsertMFADevice(ctx, username, device)\n\t\trequire.NoError(t, err, \"failed to upsert MFA device\")\n\n\t\tregisteredDevices[i] = device\n\t}\n\n\t// Verify devices were created\n\tdevices, err := authServer.GetMFADevices(ctx, username)\n\trequire.NoError(t, err, \"failed to get MFA devices\")\n\trequire.Equal(t, deviceCount, len(devices),\n\t\t\"Expected %d devices, got %d\", deviceCount, len(devices))\n\n\t// Test the bug: U2FSignRequest should return challenges for all devices,\n\t// but currently only returns a challenge for the first device.\n\tchallenge, err := authServer.U2FSignRequest(username, []byte(\"password123\"))\n\trequire.NoError(t, err, \"failed to generate U2F sign request\")\n\trequire.NotNil(t, challenge, \"expected non-nil challenge\")\n\n\t// The bug: U2FSignRequest returns a single challenge (SignRequest) instead of\n\t// challenges for all devices. The SignRequest type can only represent one device.\n\t//\n\t// WHAT THIS TEST DEMONSTRATES:\n\t// 1. We registered 3 U2F devices\n\t// 2. U2FSignRequest returns only 1 challenge\n\t// 3. That challenge is for the first device only\n\t// 4. The client cannot access/use the other registered devices\n\t//\n\t// IMPACT:\n\t// Users with multiple U2F tokens registered can only authenticate with the first one.\n\t// If that device is lost or unavailable, they have backup devices but cannot use them\n\t// because the authentication flow doesn't present them with options.\n\t//\n\t// ROOT CAUSE:\n\t// The U2FSignRequest function is designed around the old U2F API which returns\n\t// a single SignRequest.
